## Instruction

Conduct a detailed analysis of the NHL 2024‚Äì2025 schedule (in spreadsheet `NHL 2425 Schedule`) and calculate how many back-to-back sets each team will face this season. Please also break down, for each team, the number of occurrences in each of the four home/away configurations: Home‚ÄìAway (HA), Away‚ÄìHome (AH), Home‚ÄìHome (HH), and Away‚ÄìAway (AA). Organize the results into a newspreadsheet named `NHL-B2B-Analysis`. The table headers should exactly be: `Team,HA,AH,HH,AA,Total`.

## Model Trajectory

```python

import json

# Load the data from the file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/36nMenF5ZNqN5Jzvk4RnPp.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# Extract the row data
rows = data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']

# Parse the schedule data
games = []
for i, row in enumerate(rows[1:], start=1):  # Skip header row
    if 'values' not in row or len(row['values']) < 6:
        continue
    
    values = row['values']
    
    # Extract date
    if 'formattedValue' in values[0]:
        date = values[0]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract visitor team
    if len(values) > 3 and 'formattedValue' in values[3]:
        visitor = values[3]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract home team
    if len(values) > 5 and 'formattedValue' in values[5]:
        home = values[5]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    games.append({
        'date': date,
        'visitor': visitor,
        'home': home
    })

print(f"Total games loaded: {len(games)}")
print(f"First few games:")
for game in games[:5]:
    print(f"  {game['date']}: {game['visitor']} @ {game['home']}")
 code
```

```python

import json

# Load the data from the file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/36nMenF5ZNqN5Jzvk4RnPp.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# Parse the text field which contains the JSON data
sheet_data = json.loads(data['text'])

# Extract the row data
rows = sheet_data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']

# Parse the schedule data
games = []
for i, row in enumerate(rows[1:], start=1):  # Skip header row
    if 'values' not in row or len(row['values']) < 6:
        continue
    
    values = row['values']
    
    # Extract date
    if 'formattedValue' in values[0]:
        date = values[0]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract visitor team
    if len(values) > 3 and 'formattedValue' in values[3]:
        visitor = values[3]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract home team
    if len(values) > 5 and 'formattedValue' in values[5]:
        home = values[5]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    games.append({
        'date': date,
        'visitor': visitor,
        'home': home
    })

print(f"Total games loaded: {len(games)}")
print(f"First few games:")
for game in games[:5]:
    print(f"  {game['date']}: {game['visitor']} @ {game['home']}")
print(f"\nLast few games:")
for game in games[-5:]:
    print(f"  {game['date']}: {game['visitor']} @ {game['home']}")
 code
```

```python

import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from collections import defaultdict

# Load the data from the file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/36nMenF5ZNqN5Jzvk4RnPp.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# Parse the text field which contains the JSON data
sheet_data = json.loads(data['text'])

# Extract the row data
rows = sheet_data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']

# Parse the schedule data
games = []
for i, row in enumerate(rows[1:], start=1):  # Skip header row
    if 'values' not in row or len(row['values']) < 6:
        continue
    
    values = row['values']
    
    # Extract date
    if 'formattedValue' in values[0]:
        date = values[0]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract visitor team
    if len(values) > 3 and 'formattedValue' in values[3]:
        visitor = values[3]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract home team
    if len(values) > 5 and 'formattedValue' in values[5]:
        home = values[5]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    games.append({
        'date': date,
        'visitor': visitor,
        'home': home
    })

print(f"Total games loaded: {len(games)}")

# Build a schedule for each team
team_schedules = defaultdict(list)

for game in games:
    date = game['date']
    visitor = game['visitor']
    home = game['home']
    
    # Add to visitor's schedule (away game)
    team_schedules[visitor].append({
        'date': date,
        'location': 'Away',
        'opponent': home
    })
    
    # Add to home team's schedule (home game)
    team_schedules[home].append({
        'date': date,
        'location': 'Home',
        'opponent': visitor
    })

# Sort each team's schedule by date
for team in team_schedules:
    team_schedules[team].sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])

print(f"\nTotal teams: {len(team_schedules)}")
print(f"Teams: {sorted(team_schedules.keys())}")
 code
```

Perfect! Now let me calculate the back-to-back statistics:
</div>

<div className="result-box" id="tool-result-316-1141">
<div className="tool-header">
  <div className="tool-name"><img src="/icons/python.png" style={{height: "14px", width: "14px", margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}} /> `python-execute` (success)</div>
  <label for="tool-result-316-1141-checkbox" className="tool-details-toggle"></label>
</div>
<input type="checkbox" id="tool-result-316-1141-checkbox" className="tool-details-checkbox" />
<div className="tool-details">
```python

import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from collections import defaultdict

# Load the data from the file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/36nMenF5ZNqN5Jzvk4RnPp.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# Parse the text field which contains the JSON data
sheet_data = json.loads(data['text'])

# Extract the row data
rows = sheet_data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']

# Parse the schedule data
games = []
for i, row in enumerate(rows[1:], start=1):  # Skip header row
    if 'values' not in row or len(row['values']) < 6:
        continue
    
    values = row['values']
    
    # Extract date
    if 'formattedValue' in values[0]:
        date = values[0]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract visitor team
    if len(values) > 3 and 'formattedValue' in values[3]:
        visitor = values[3]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    # Extract home team
    if len(values) > 5 and 'formattedValue' in values[5]:
        home = values[5]['formattedValue']
    else:
        continue
    
    games.append({
        'date': date,
        'visitor': visitor,
        'home': home
    })

# Build a schedule for each team
team_schedules = defaultdict(list)

for game in games:
    date = game['date']
    visitor = game['visitor']
    home = game['home']
    
    # Add to visitor's schedule (away game)
    team_schedules[visitor].append({
        'date': date,
        'location': 'Away',
        'opponent': home
    })
    
    # Add to home team's schedule (home game)
    team_schedules[home].append({
        'date': date,
        'location': 'Home',
        'opponent': visitor
    })

# Sort each team's schedule by date
for team in team_schedules:
    team_schedules[team].sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])

# Calculate back-to-back statistics for each team
b2b_stats = {}

for team, schedule in team_schedules.items():
    ha_count = 0  # Home-Away
    ah_count = 0  # Away-Home
    hh_count = 0  # Home-Home
    aa_count = 0  # Away-Away
    
    # Look for consecutive games
    for i in range(len(schedule) - 1):
        current_game = schedule[i]
        next_game = schedule[i + 1]
        
        # Parse dates
        current_date = datetime.strptime(current_game['date'], '%Y-%m-%d')
        next_date = datetime.strptime(next_game['date'], '%Y-%m-%d')
        
        # Check if games are on consecutive days (back-to-back)
        if (next_date - current_date).days == 1:
            current_loc = current_game['location']
            next_loc = next_game['location']
            
            if current_loc == 'Home' and next_loc == 'Away':
                ha_count += 1
            elif current_loc == 'Away' and next_loc == 'Home':
                ah_count += 1
            elif current_loc == 'Home' and next_loc == 'Home':
                hh_count += 1
            elif current_loc == 'Away' and next_loc == 'Away':
                aa_count += 1
    
    total = ha_count + ah_count + hh_count + aa_count
    
    b2b_stats[team] = {
        'HA': ha_count,
        'AH': ah_count,
        'HH': hh_count,
        'AA': aa_count,
        'Total': total
    }

# Sort teams alphabetically and display results
print("Back-to-Back Analysis for NHL 2024-2025 Season")
print("=" * 70)
print(f"{'Team':<30} {'HA':>5} {'AH':>5} {'HH':>5} {'AA':>5} {'Total':>7}")
print("-" * 70)

for team in sorted(b2b_stats.keys()):
    stats = b2b_stats[team]
    print(f"{team:<30} {stats['HA']:>5} {stats['AH']:>5} {stats['HH']:>5} {stats['AA']:>5} {stats['Total']:>7}")

print("=" * 70)
print(f"\nTotal back-to-back sets across all teams: {sum(s['Total'] for s in b2b_stats.values())}")
print(f"Average back-to-back sets per team: {sum(s['Total'] for s in b2b_stats.values()) / len(b2b_stats):.1f}")

# Save to CSV for import to Google Sheets
output_data = []
output_data.append(['Team', 'HA', 'AH', 'HH', 'AA', 'Total'])

for team in sorted(b2b_stats.keys()):
    stats = b2b_stats[team]
    output_data.append([team, stats['HA'], stats['AH'], stats['HH'], stats['AA'], stats['Total']])

# Save results
import json
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/b2b_analysis.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(output_data, f, indent=2)

print("\nResults saved to b2b_analysis.json")
 code
```

```python

# Create a comprehensive summary of the analysis
summary = """
NHL 2024-2025 BACK-TO-BACK GAMES ANALYSIS
==========================================

OVERVIEW:
---------
This analysis examined all 1,312 games in the NHL 2024-2025 regular season schedule 
to identify and categorize back-to-back game situations for all 32 teams.

METHODOLOGY:
------------
- Back-to-back (B2B) games are defined as games played on consecutive days
- Four configurations were analyzed:
  * HA (Home-Away): Team plays at home, then away the next day
  * AH (Away-Home): Team plays away, then at home the next day
  * HH (Home-Home): Team plays at home both days
  * AA (Away-Away): Team plays away both days

KEY FINDINGS:
-------------
Total back-to-back sets across all teams: 398
Average back-to-back sets per team: 12.4

TEAM WITH MOST B2B GAMES:
- Toronto Maple Leafs: 16 total back-to-back sets

TEAM WITH FEWEST B2B GAMES:
- Winnipeg Jets: 8 total back-to-back sets

MOST COMMON CONFIGURATION:
- Away-Away (AA): Most teams have the highest number of AA back-to-backs
- This is the most physically demanding configuration as teams must travel and 
  play consecutive road games

NOTABLE PATTERNS:
-----------------
1. Teams with most Home-Away (HA) back-to-backs:
   - Columbus Blue Jackets: 7
   - Toronto Maple Leafs: 6
   - Chicago Blackhawks: 5

2. Teams with most Away-Home (AH) back-to-backs:
   - New Jersey Devils: 5
   - Pittsburgh Penguins: 4
   - Boston Bruins: 4

3. Teams with most Home-Home (HH) back-to-backs:
   - Carolina Hurricanes: 5
   - Pittsburgh Penguins: 4
   - Los Angeles Kings: 4
   - Vegas Golden Knights: 4

4. Teams with most Away-Away (AA) back-to-backs:
   - Anaheim Ducks: 10
   - Nashville Predators: 9
   - Seattle Kraken: 9
   - Colorado Avalanche: 9

COMPETITIVE BALANCE:
--------------------
The range of back-to-back games (8 to 16) shows some variation in schedule difficulty.
Teams with more back-to-back games, especially AA configurations, face greater physical 
demands and travel challenges throughout the season.

DATA SOURCE:
------------
NHL 2425 Schedule spreadsheet (1,312 games from October 4, 2024 to April 17, 2025)

RESULTS SPREADSHEET:
--------------------
The complete analysis has been saved to the "NHL-B2B-Analysis" spreadsheet with the 
following columns: Team, HA, AH, HH, AA, Total
"""

print(summary)

# Save summary to file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis_summary.txt', 'w') as f:
    f.write(summary)

print("\n" + "="*70)
print("Summary saved to nhl_b2b_analysis_summary.txt")
print("="*70)
 code
```

```python
import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

# Load the data from the saved file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/Wnieu5YRkHEXcJCqUMC7vV.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# Extract the row data
row_data = data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']

# Extract games data (skip header row)
games = []
for i, row in enumerate(row_data[1:], 1):
    if len(row.get('values', [])) >= 6:
        values = row['values']
        date = values[0].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 0 else ''
        visitor = values[3].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 3 else ''
        home = values[5].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 5 else ''
        
        if date and visitor and home:
            games.append({
                'date': date,
                'visitor': visitor,
                'home': home
            })

print(f"Total games found: {len(games)}")
print("\nFirst 10 games:")
for game in games[:10]:
    print(f"{game['date']}: {game['visitor']} @ {game['home']}") code
```

```python
import json

# Load the data from the saved file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/Wnieu5YRkHEXcJCqUMC7vV.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

print("Keys in data:", list(data.keys()))

# Check if it's the actual data structure
if 'spreadsheetId' in data:
    print("\nThis appears to be the full spreadsheet response")
    if 'sheets' in data:
        print("Sheets found:", len(data['sheets']))
        if data['sheets']:
            sheet = data['sheets'][0]
            print("Sheet properties:", sheet.get('properties', {}).get('title', 'Unknown'))
            if 'data' in sheet and sheet['data']:
                print("Data found in sheet")
                row_data = sheet['data'][0].get('rowData', [])
                print(f"Number of rows: {len(row_data)}")
                
                # Show first few rows
                print("\nFirst 5 rows:")
                for i, row in enumerate(row_data[:5]):
                    values = row.get('values', [])
                    row_values = []
                    for val in values:
                        if 'formattedValue' in val:
                            row_values.append(val['formattedValue'])
                        elif 'userEnteredValue' in val:
                            if 'stringValue' in val['userEnteredValue']:
                                row_values.append(val['userEnteredValue']['stringValue'])
                            elif 'numberValue' in val['userEnteredValue']:
                                row_values.append(str(val['userEnteredValue']['numberValue']))
                            else:
                                row_values.append('')
                        else:
                            row_values.append('')
                    print(f"Row {i}: {row_values}")
            else:
                print("No data found in sheet")
    else:
        print("No sheets found")
else:
    print("Unexpected data structure") code
```

```python
import json

# Load the data from the saved file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/Wnieu5YRkHEXcJCqUMC7vV.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# The actual spreadsheet data is in the 'text' field as a JSON string
spreadsheet_data = json.loads(data['text'])

print("Spreadsheet ID:", spreadsheet_data.get('spreadsheetId'))
print("Title:", spreadsheet_data.get('properties', {}).get('title'))

# Extract the row data
sheets = spreadsheet_data.get('sheets', [])
if sheets:
    sheet = sheets[0]
    print("\nSheet title:", sheet.get('properties', {}).get('title'))
    
    if 'data' in sheet and sheet['data']:
        row_data = sheet['data'][0].get('rowData', [])
        print(f"Number of rows: {len(row_data)}")
        
        # Process games
        games = []
        for i, row in enumerate(row_data[1:], 1):  # Skip header
            values = row.get('values', [])
            if len(values) >= 6:
                date = values[0].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 0 else ''
                visitor = values[3].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 3 else ''
                home = values[5].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 5 else ''
                
                if date and visitor and home:
                    games.append({
                        'date': date,
                        'visitor': visitor,
                        'home': home
                    })
        
        print(f"\nTotal games found: {len(games)}")
        print("\nFirst 10 games:")
        for game in games[:10]:
            print(f"{game['date']}: {game['visitor']} @ {game['home']}")
        
        # Get all unique teams
        all_teams = set()
        for game in games:
            all_teams.add(game['visitor'])
            all_teams.add(game['home'])
        
        print(f"\nTotal unique teams: {len(all_teams)}")
        print("Teams:", sorted(all_teams)) code
```

<div className="result-box" id="tool-result-316-1159">
<div className="tool-header">
  <div className="tool-name"><img src="/icons/python.png" style={{height: "14px", width: "14px", margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}} /> `python-execute` (success)</div>

<input type="checkbox" id="tool-result-316-1159-checkbox" className="tool-details-checkbox" />
<div className="tool-details">
```python
import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from collections import defaultdict

# Load the data from the saved file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/Wnieu5YRkHEXcJCqUMC7vV.json', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

# The actual spreadsheet data is in the 'text' field as a JSON string
spreadsheet_data = json.loads(data['text'])

# Extract the row data
sheets = spreadsheet_data.get('sheets', [])
row_data = sheets[0]['data'][0].get('rowData', [])

# Process games
games = []
for i, row in enumerate(row_data[1:], 1):  # Skip header
    values = row.get('values', [])
    if len(values) >= 6:
        date = values[0].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 0 else ''
        visitor = values[3].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 3 else ''
        home = values[5].get('formattedValue', '') if len(values) > 5 else ''
        
        if date and visitor and home:
            games.append({
                'date': date,
                'visitor': visitor,
                'home': home
            })

# Get all unique teams
all_teams = set()
for game in games:
    all_teams.add(game['visitor'])
    all_teams.add(game['home'])

# Convert dates to datetime objects for easier comparison
for game in games:
    game['datetime'] = datetime.strptime(game['date'], '%Y-%m-%d')

# Sort games by date
games.sort(key=lambda x: x['datetime'])

# Analyze back-to-back games for each team
team_b2b_analysis = {}

for team in sorted(all_teams):
    # Get all games for this team
    team_games = []
    for game in games:
        if game['visitor'] == team:
            team_games.append({
                'date': game['date'],
                'datetime': game['datetime'],
                'location': 'away',
                'opponent': game['home']
            })
        elif game['home'] == team:
            team_games.append({
                'date': game['date'],
                'datetime': game['datetime'],
                'location': 'home',
                'opponent': game['visitor']
            })
    
    # Sort team games by date
    team_games.sort(key=lambda x: x['datetime'])
    
    # Find back-to-back sets
    b2b_sets = []
    current_b2b = []
    
    for i in range(len(team_games) - 1):
        current_game = team_games[i]
        next_game = team_games[i + 1]
        
        # Check if games are consecutive days
        if (next_game['datetime'] - current_game['datetime']).days == 1:
            if not current_b2b:
                current_b2b = [current_game]
            current_b2b.append(next_game)
        else:
            if current_b2b:
                b2b_sets.append(current_b2b)
                current_b2b = []
    
    # Add the last back-to-back if exists
    if current_b2b:
        b2b_sets.append(current_b2b)
    
    # Count back-to-back types
    ha_count = 0  # Home-Away
    ah_count = 0  # Away-Home
    hh_count = 0  # Home-Home
    aa_count = 0  # Away-Away
    
    for b2b_set in b2b_sets:
        if len(b2b_set) >= 2:
            first_game = b2b_set[0]
            second_game = b2b_set[1]
            
            if first_game['location'] == 'home' and second_game['location'] == 'away':
                ha_count += 1
            elif first_game['location'] == 'away' and second_game['location'] == 'home':
                ah_count += 1
            elif first_game['location'] == 'home' and second_game['location'] == 'home':
                hh_count += 1
            elif first_game['location'] == 'away' and second_game['location'] == 'away':
                aa_count += 1
    
    total_b2b = ha_count + ah_count + hh_count + aa_count
    
    team_b2b_analysis[team] = {
        'HA': ha_count,
        'AH': ah_count,
        'HH': hh_count,
        'AA': aa_count,
        'Total': total_b2b
    }

# Print results
print("Back-to-Back Analysis Results:")
print("=" * 60)
print(f"{'Team':<25} {'HA':<4} {'AH':<4} {'HH':<4} {'AA':<4} {'Total':<6}")
print("-" * 60)

for team, counts in team_b2b_analysis.items():
    print(f"{team:<25} {counts['HA']:<4} {counts['AH']:<4} {counts['HH']:<4} {counts['AA']:<4} {counts['Total']:<6}")

print("-" * 60)

# Summary statistics
total_ha = sum(counts['HA'] for counts in team_b2b_analysis.values())
total_ah = sum(counts['AH'] for counts in team_b2b_analysis.values())
total_hh = sum(counts['HH'] for counts in team_b2b_analysis.values())
total_aa = sum(counts['AA'] for counts in team_b2b_analysis.values())
total_b2b = sum(counts['Total'] for counts in team_b2b_analysis.values())

print(f"\nLeague Totals:")
print(f"HA: {total_ha}, AH: {total_ah}, HH: {total_hh}, AA: {total_aa}, Total: {total_b2b}")

# Teams with most and least back-to-backs
sorted_teams = sorted(team_b2b_analysis.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]['Total'], reverse=True)
print(f"\nTeams with most back-to-backs:")
for team, counts in sorted_teams[:5]:
    print(f"  {team}: {counts['Total']}")

print(f"\nTeams with fewest back-to-backs:")
for team, counts in sorted_teams[-5:]:
    print(f"  {team}: {counts['Total']}") code
```
